Jamison Brereton

29 (383)
Indra
Gauriv─лti ┼Ъ─Бktya
15 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
This hymn consists primarily of a recital of IndraтАЩs great deeds, with special atten tion to the Vr╠еtra saga and the MarutsтАЩ role in it (vss. 1тАУ4, 6тАУ9). Interspersed are verses devoted to two much less understood myths, IndraтАЩs conflict with the Sun in an apparent chariot race (vss. 5, 9тАУ10) and his journey with Kutsa to U┼Ыan─БтАЩs house and the defeat of ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa (vs. 9), myths that often appear together and show narrative connections. There are as well brief mentions of other exploits of Indra, including the Vala myth (vs. 12). The story of the SunтАЩs chariot and the Kutsa/U┼Ыan─Б complex are particular preoccupations of the Indra hymns of Maс╣Зс╕Нala V, although the refer ences to them (SunтАЩs chariot V.31.11, Kutsa/U┼Ыan─Б V.31.7тАУ10) do not help to clarify the details as much as we would like.
The poet several times (vss. 1, 3, 7) mentions Manu, the first ─Аrya man and sac rificer, in connection with the mythic past. This emphasis on Manu, the theoretical ancestor of the current sacrificers, is presumably meant to associate those current sacrificers with the participants and supporters of Indra in his previous deeds, in order to gain a portion of reflected glory. As often, the hymn sometimes narrates the myths as if in present time (see esp. vss. 1, 6, 12, all three using the same verb тАЬthey chantтАЭ [├бrcanti]). This again is a strategy serving the same purpose, here by specifically identifying the present singers with both the Maruts and the Aс╣Еgirases.
The hymn is also structured by recurrent soma-drinking phrases, each slightly different, almost always in the second half of an even p─Бda (see 2b, 3b, 3d, 5b, 7d, 8b, 11d), a pattern that provides a sort of rhythmic theme-and-variations.
It ends with three verses (13тАУ15) in which the poet refers globally to the amaz ing range of IndraтАЩs deeds past and future, and in the final verse offers him his own well-crafted poems. Only one word in this verse, vas┼лy├║с╕е тАЬseeking goods,тАЭ out of the whole hymn, hints that the poet would like something in return.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra As noted in the published introduction, the hymn is punctuated by expressions of somadrinking, each slightly different and generally found in the 2nd half of an even p─Бda: 2b … papiv─Б╠Бс╣Гsaс╣Г sut├бsya 3b … s├│masya s├║с╣гutasya pey─Бс╕е 3d … papiv─Б╠Бm ├нndro asya [rhyming with 2b] 5b … somap├йyam [cf. 3b] [7d sut├бm pibat … s├│mam] 8b … somy─Б╠Бp─Б╠Бс╕е 11d … ├бpibaс╕е s├│mam asya

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIn the adoration of the gods by Manu there are three effulgences, and they, (the Maruts), uphold three luminaries in heaven; the Maruts of pure energy worship you, for you, Indra, are their intelligent с╣Ыс╣гiтАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Three luminaries: the sun, the wind, and fire; the same trio may be intended by the earlier phrase tryaryam─Б tr─лс╣Зi aryam─Бс╣Зi tej─Бс╣Гsi

Jamison Brereton

They uphold the three customs [=rituals of the soma-pressing day] at ManuтАЩs attendance on the gods and the three heavenly realms of light. The Maruts of refined skill chant to you. You are their wise seer, Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I follow Brereton (─Аdityas, 165-66), who in turn followed Thieme (Mitra and Aryaman, 78-77), in taking aryam─Б╠Бnot as nom. sg. masc. (as it is normally and as taken by the standard tr.), but as acc. pl. neut. construed with tr─л╠Б(like tr─л╠Бrocan─Б╠Бin the next p─Бda). Against ThiemeтАЩs тАЬthree hospitalities,тАЭ Brereton plausibly suggests that in this context the three aryam─Б╠Бmust refer to тАЬwhat governs the ritual,тАЭ perhaps the three soma-pressings or the three fires.

P─Бda-initial tr─л╠Б, found here in a and b, recurs in 7c, 8a, b (also non-initial in 7b).

In c p┼лt├б-dakс╣гa- (/p┼лt├б-dakс╣гas-) is ordinarily ─Аdityan vocabulary (though used of the Maruts also in VIII.94.7, 10). Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) supply the ─Аdityas as the subj. of dh─Бrayanta in b and of course take Aryaman as the subject of p─Бda a. By contrast, I think the Maruts are subjects of all three p─Бdas – but they are identified with the ─Аdityas throughout, as the use of p┼лt├бdakс╣гa-, ordinarily a qualifier of the ─Аdityas, makes clear.

Griffith

MAN’S worship of the Gods hath three great lustres, and three celestial lights have they established
The Maruts gifted with pure strength adore thee, for thou, O Indra, art their sapient Rsi.

Geldner

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen the Maruts worship Indra, exulting and drinking of the effused libation, he grasps the thunderbolt wherewith he destroys Ahi, and sets the abundant waters free to flow.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When the Maruts chanted to him after he became exhilarated, to Indra who had drunk of the pressed soma,
he took up the mace. When he (had) smashed the serpent, he released the exuberant waters to flow.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take abh├н y├бd ├бhim han as subordinate to ─Б╠Бdatta v├бjram in the same p─Бda. Although this fits the metrical scheme slightly better, it makes some trouble with the logical sequence of events (тАЬhe took the mace when he smashed the serpent,тАЭ almost implying that the smashing occurred first). It works better as subordinate to the main clause of d.

The word order ├бhim h├бn and the lack of augment on the verb scrambles the standard formula, producing almost a syncopated effect, which is repaired in 3d.

Griffith

What time the Maruts sang their song to Indra, joyous when he had drunk of Soma juices,
He grasped his thunderbolt to slay the Dragon, and loosed, that they might flow, the youthful Waters.

Geldner

Als die Marut dem trankbegeisterten Indra zusangen, der vom Soma getrunken hatte, da fa├Яte er die Keule, als er den Drachen erschlug. Er lie├Я die j├╝ngstgeborenen Gew├дsser frei zum Laufen.

Grassmann

Als ihm, dem frohen, zu die Maruts jauchzten, dem Indra, da vom Safte er getrunken, Da nahm den Blitz er und erschlug die Schlange, ergoss die schnellen Wasser, dass sie str├╢mten.

Elizarenkova

рдЙрддрд╛рдкрд┐рдЪ рд╣реЗрдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордгреЛрдмреГрд╣рдиреНрддреЛрд╣реЗрдорд░реБрддреЛрдпреВрдпрдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рд╢реНрдЪ рд╕реБрд╕реБрддрд╕реНрдп рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБрдЕрднрд┐рд╖реБрддрд╕реНрдп рдореЗ рдорджреАрдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрдп рд╕реЛрдорд╕реНрдп рдЗрдордВрд╕реЛрдордВ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрд╖рд╖реНрдареА рдкреЗрдпрд╛рдГ рдкрд┐рдмрдд рдкрд┐рдмрддреЗрд░рд╛рд╢реАрд░реНрд▓рд┐рдЩрд┐рдордзреНрдпрдордмрд╣реБрд╡рдЪрдирд╕реНрдпреИрдХрд╡рдЪрдирдВ рддрджреНрдзрд┐ рддрддрдЦрд▓реБ рд╣рд╡реНрдпрдВ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рдГрдкреАрддрдВрд╕реЛрдорд╛рддреНрдордХрдВрд╣рд╡рд┐рдГ рдордиреБрд╖реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдп рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдп рдЧрд╛рдГ рдзреЗрдиреВрдГ рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рдиреНрдпреБрджрдХрд╛рдирд┐ рд╡рд╛ рдЕрд╡рд┐рдиреНрджрддреН рд╡реЗрджрдпрддрд┐ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдЩреНрдЧрд╛рд▓рдореНрднрдпрддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪрд╛рд╕реНрдпреЗрдордВрд╕реЛрдордореНрдк рдкрд┐рд╡рд╛рдиреН рдкреАрддрд╡рд╛рдирд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдЕрд╣рд┐рдВрд╡реГрддреНрд░рдВ рдЕрд╣рдиреН рдЕрд╡рдзреАрддреН рее рей рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOr,mighty Maruts, and you also, Indra, drink of this my copiously-effused libation; then the offered libation obtains cattle for the offerer, and Indra, drinking of it, kills Ahi.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Obtains cattle for the offerer: m─Бnuс╣гe g─Б avindat = yajam─Бnasya vedayati g─Б may also mean rain, dhenuvс╣Ыс╣гс╣нilakс╣гaс╣З─Бni udak─Бni v─Б

Jamison Brereton

AndтАФyou formulators, you MarutsтАФIndra should drink of this well-pressed soma of mine,
for this is his oblation: he found the cows for Manu; Indra smashed the serpent, having drunk of it.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take havy├бm as the subj. of ├бvindat: тАЬthe oblation found the cows for Manu.тАЭ This interpr. accounts for the accent on ├бvindat, which would be generated by h├н. But it is otherwise bizarre: g─Б╠Бс╕е тИЪvid тАШfind the cowsтАЩ is a standard formula in the Vala myth, and the subject of the verb is always Indra or his agent(s)/companion(s) (e.g., Aс╣Еgirases I.62.2, Saram─Б V.45.7, 8); for Indra himself cf., e.g., I.101.5, II.19.3, VIII.96.17, and in a variant of the formula in the next hymn

Griffith

And, O ye Brahmans, Maruts, so may Indra drink draughts of this my carefully pressed Sorna;
For this oblation found for man the cattle, and Indra, having quaffed it, slew the Dragon.

Geldner

Auch von dem meinigen, von dem wohlgepre├Яten Soma soll Indra trinken, ihr erbaulich redenden Marut, denn diese Opferspende fand f├╝r die Manu die Rinder. Indra erschlug den Drachen, nachdem er davon getrunken hatte.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThereupon he fixed firmly heaven and earth, and resolutely advancing, filled (Vс╣Ыtra), like a deer, with terror, stripping off his covering, Indra, slew the D─Бnava, endeavouring to hide, and panting with affright.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

After that he propped the two world-halves wide apart; even while enwrapped, he set the wild beast to fearing.
Repeatedly taunting the gulper, Indra smashed the snorting D─Бnava back and down.

Jamison Brereton Notes

For Indra enwrapped in the earth, cf. I.173.6 s├бс╣Г vivya ├нndro vrj├бna ╠е с╣Г n├б bh┼л╠Бma тАЬIndra has enwrapped himself in the earth like a girth.тАЭ Cf. also his wearing the earth III.32.11, VIII.4.8. Although here the enwrapping seems presented as a handicap, esp. given the cid, in the just cited passages the images seem rather to emphasize IndraтАЩs vastness.

As noted also by Geldner, Schaeffer, and Witzel Got┼Н, j├нgartim тАж apaj├бrgur─Бс╣Зaс╕е is a word play, but the words presumably belong to different roots. The first is universally assigned to тИЪgс╣Э тАШswallowтАЩ, but the root affiliation of the second is disputed. Geldner and EWA (s.v. GAR─л p. 470) assign it to a тИЪgс╣Э тАШhold outтАЩ, but I follow Schaeffer (Intens., 116-22) in taking it to тИЪgс╣Э тАШgreet, extolтАЩ, with the negative sense contributed by the preverb ├бpa. So also Witzel Got┼Н and Oberlies (Relig. I.401). See also nearby apag┼л╠Бrya (V.32.6).

The etymological separation of j├нgartim and apaj├бrgur─Бс╣Зaс╕е invites further scrutiny of the hapax j├нgartim. As noted above, this word is generally grouped with тИЪgс╣Э тАШswallowтАЩ and interpreted as an agent noun тАШswallowerтАЩ (my тАШgulperтАЩ). However, with apaj├бrgur─Бс╣Зaс╕е off the table, there is no particular contextual support for this interpr., though it is certainly semantically acceptable. Far more troubling are the serious formal problems. For one thing, -ti- is by no means an agent-noun suffix; it normally of course forms feminine abstracts, though AiG II.2.636-37 does register a number of such stems that have been reanalyzed тАЬzur Bez. der pers├╢nlichen Tr├дger des Verbalbegriffs zu verwenden.тАЭ Debrunner himself identifies our form as a 3rd sg.

verb form inflected as a -ti-stem (AiG II.2.638), but this interpr. has nothing to recommend it. Not only is such a morphological transfer not a feature of the RV, but there is also no such verb stem available to be nominalized. The root тИЪgс╣Э тАШswallowтАЩ does not have a redupl. pres. or in fact any redupl. stem save for the pf. jag─Бra and the intensive subj. jalgulas (I.28.1); the single form of the redupl. aor. aj─лgar (I.163.7) supposedly belonging to this root (see Grassmann, and Whit. Roots) actually belongs with the other forms of this stem to the root тИЪgс╣Э тАШawakenтАЩ, and we just discussed intens. part. j├бrgur─Бс╣Зa- above. It is, further, a seс╣н root; itтАЩs hard to know what its pre-C full grade should be in a redupl. pres. formation since there are no parallel formations to roots in -с╣Э that I know of (*j├нgar─лti? cf. VS galgal─лti and EWA s.vv. GARI2 , GAL), but presumably not simply gar. In short, neither the nominal morphology nor the root formation of j├нgarti- is easily accounted for under the standard hypothesis, but I have nothing better to substitute. I therefore retain the rendering in the published translation, though with full awareness of its fragility. My thanks to Veronique Kremmer, who drew my attention to j├нgarti- and its many problems and discussed the issues at length with me.

тАЬThen, for this exploit, all the gods gave you Maghavan, in succession, the Soma beverage; whence you have retarded, for the sake of Eta┼Ыa, the advancing horses of the sun.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Then according to your will, o bounteous one, all the gods conceded the soma-drinking to you,
when you put the flying golden mares of the Sun behind, though they were in front, in (the presence of) Eta┼Ыa.

Griffith

Thus all the Gods, O Maghavan, delivered to thee of their free will the draught of Soma;
When thou for Etasa didst cause to tarry the flying mares of Surya racing forward.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhereupon Maghavan has destroyed with his thunderbolt at once his (┼Ъambara’s) ninety and nine cities; the Maruts glorifying Indra in a common dwelling with the Triс╣гс╣нubh hymn, he destroyed the bright (city of the asura).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Cities: the text has bhog─Бn = cities, bhog─Бn ityantod─Бttaс╕е purav─Бcanaс╕е

Jamison Brereton

When the bounteous one hews apart his [=Vr╠еtraтАЩs] nine and ninety coils at one blow with his mace,
the Maruts chant to Indra at the seat (of conflict). With speech in
triс╣гс╣нubh meter he thrusts heaven (away from earth).

Jamison Brereton Notes

IndraтАЩs two actions in this vs. are expressed by injunctives (vivс╣Ы┼Ыc├бt b, b─Бdhata d), as in the preceding vs. (kaс╕е 5d), but the middle verb, ├бrcanti in c, is emphatically present. The configuration here, #├бrcant─л╠Бndram mar├║taс╕е, matches that of 1c #├бrcanti tv─Б mar├║taс╕е. See Hoffmann (Injunk. 165) on this vs., who seems to think the тАЬtimeless, mentioningтАЭ function of the injunctive can be so distant from a real preterite that it can drag in present indicatives. I would attribute it rather to the attempt in this hymn to associate the heroic deeds of the past with the activities of the present sacrificers. It is also barely possible that the text originally read

*├бrcant├нndram, that is, *├бrcant ├нndram with the underlying 3rd pl. ending -nt preserved before vowel, but later reint. as pres. -nti after -nt regularly became -nn.

The -├н- could then have been lengthened, as if a sandhi product of ├бrcanti ├нndram, with no metrical consequences. The change would have been facilitated by the model of likewise p─Бda-initial ├бrcanti in 1c, as well as arcanti in 12b. Still, on balance I find this unlikely. Other examples of preserved -nt because of early misparsing as -nti occur before the enclitic pronoun ─лm, and the result in either case would be -nt─лm. See disc. ad I.67.4, etc.

Griffith

When Maghavan with the thunderbolt demolished his nine-and-ninety castles all together,
The Maruts, where they met, glorified Indra: ye with the Trstup hymn obstructed heaven.

Geldner

Als der Gabenreiche dessen neunundneunzig Windungen auf einmal mit der Keule zerhieb, da besingen die Marut den Indra auf der Stelle. Durch die Tristubhrede trieb er den Himmel in die Enge.

Grassmann

Als er des D├дmons neunundneunzig Schanzen der starke mit dem Blitz zerbrach auf einmal тАУ Den Indra preisen auf dem Sitz die Maruts тАУ so schlug den Himmel er mit lautem Jubel.

Elizarenkova

рд╕рдЦрд╛ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдпрдорд┐рддреНрд░рднреВрддреЛрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рдорд╣рд┐рд╖рд╛ рдорд╣рд┐рд╖рд╛рдгрд╛рдореНрдкрд╢реВрдирд╛рдВ рддреНрд░реА рддреНрд░реАрдгрд┐ рд╢рддрд╛рдирд┐ рд╢рддрд╕рдЩреНрдЦреНрдпрд╛рдХрд╛рдирд┐ рд╕рдЦреНрдпреЗ рд╕рдЦреНрдпреБрд░реНрдорд┐рддреНрд░рднреВрддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрдпреЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдХреНрд░рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрднреВрддреЗрди рддреВрдпрдВ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдВ рдЕрдкрдЪрддреН рдкрдкрд╛рдЪ рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГрдкрд░рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдпреБрдХреНрддрдГ рдордиреБрд╖реЛрдордиреЛрдГрд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдзреАрдирд┐ рддреНрд░реА рддреНрд░реАрдгрд┐рд╕рд░рд╛рдВрд╕рд┐ рдкрд╛рддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рдЕрддреНрд░рд╕рд░рд╕реН рд╢рдмреНрджреЗрди рдкреВрддрднреГрджрд╛рдзрд╡рдиреАрдпрджреНрд░реЛрдгрдХрд▓рд╢рд╕рдЮреНрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд┐рдкрд╛рддреНрд░рд╛рдгреНрдпреБрдЪреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рддреЗрд╖реБрд╕реНрдерд┐рддрдВрд╕реБрддрдо рднрд┐рд╖реБрддрдВрд╕реЛрдордВрд╕рд╛рдХрдВ рдпреБрдЧрдкрджреЗрд╡ рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╣рддреНрдпрд╛рдп рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╣рдирдирд╛рдп рдкрд┐рдмрджрдкрд┐рдмрддреН рдкрдкреМ рее рен рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTo aid (the undertaking of) his friend, Agni, the friend (of Indra) has quickly consumed three hundred buffaloes; and Indra, for the destruction of Vс╣Ыtra, has at once quaffed vessels of Soma, offered by Manu.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Has quickly consumed: apacat, has roasted or digested

Jamison Brereton

As a comrade for a comrade, Agni straightaway cooked three hundred buffalo in accord with his [=IndraтАЩs] will.
Indra drank the pressed soma of Manu, three lakes worth at one blow, for the Vr╠еtra-smashing.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On neut. pl. mahiс╣г─Б╠Бin conjunction with the numerical expression tr─л╠Б┼Ыat─Б╠Бni see Oldenberg Note the alternative phrasing with gen. pl. in 8a tr─л╠БтАж ┼Ыat─Б╠Бmahiс╣г─Б╠Бс╣З─Бm.

Griffith

As friend to aid a friend, Agni dressed quickly three hundred buffaloes, even as he willed it.
And Indra, from man’s gift, for Vrtra’s slaughter, drank ofr at once three lakes of pressed-out Soma.

Geldner

Der Freund Agni kochte dem Freund sogleich nach dessen Wunsch dreihundert B├╝ffel. Indra trank den gepre├Яten Soma des Manu, drei Seen auf einmal aus zur Vritrat├╢tung.

Grassmann

Und Agni briet in Eil’ der Freund dem Freunde dreihundert B├╝ffel mit der Kraft, die sein ist; Dazu trank Indra den gepressten Soma, drei Seen der Menschen aus zur Vritrat├╢dtung.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╕рдЦрд╛) рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдореН (рд╕рдЦреНрдпреЗ) (рдЕрдкрдЪрддреН) рдкрдЪрддрд┐ (рддреВрдпрдореН) рддреВрд░реНрдгрдореН (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ) рдкрд╛рд╡рдХрдГ (рдЕрд╕реНрдп) (рдХреНрд░рддреНрд╡рд╛) рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрдпрд╛ рдХрд░реНрдореНрдордгрд╛ рд╡рд╛ (рдорд╣рд┐рд╖рд╛) рдорд╣рд┐рд╖рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдорд╣рддрд╛рдореН рдкрд╢реВрдирд╛рдореН (рддреНрд░реА) рддреНрд░реАрдгрд┐ (рд╢рддрд╛рдирд┐) (рддреНрд░реА) (рд╕рд╛рдХрдореН) (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ) рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрдГ (рдордиреБрд╖рдГ) рдордиреБрд╖рд╕реНрдп (рд╕рд░рд╛рдВрд╕рд┐) рддрдбрд╛рдЧрд╛рдиреН (рд╕реБрддрдореН) рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд┐рддрдореН (рдкрд┐рдмрддреН) рдкрд┐рдмрддрд┐ (рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╣рддреНрдпрд╛рдп) рдореЗрдШрд╕реНрдп рд╣рдирдирд╛рдп (рд╕реЛрдордореН) рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдореН рееренрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen you had eaten the flesh of the three hundred buffaloes, when you who are Maghavan had drunk the three vessels of Soma, when he had slain Ahi, then all the gods summoned Indra, full of food, as if he had been a servant, to the battle.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

When he had slain Ahi: or perhaps yad ahim jagh─Бna, that he should kill Ahi

Jamison Brereton

When you the bounteous devoured the flesh of three hundred buffaloes and drank three somian lakes,
all the gods called тАЬCarry (the day)!тАЭ to Indra as (a gambler calls)
тАЬGame!,тАЭ when he smashed the serpent.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Grassmann and Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н] take both ├бghaс╕е and ├бp─Бс╕е as 3rd sg. Since ├бghas belongs to the root pres. to тИЪghas, either 2nd or 3rd sg. is grammatically possible. But for ├бp─Бс╕е to be 3rd sg., an s-aor. stem ├бp─Бs- has to be posited, for which there is no other support save for a med. p─Бsta in a m─Б╠Б-prohibitive in the AV (XII.3.43). Nevertheless, Narten does set up such a stem (Sig.Aor. 168). I see no reason to do so; the presence of nom. sg. magh├бv─Б, adduced as evidence by Narten, is not sufficient, since nom. sg.

appositives to 2nd sg. subjects are common. Also common is abrupt shifting between 2nd and 3rd ps., found already in this hymn between vss. 1 and 2, 4 and 5, 5 and 6. In our vs. we must assume that a shift happens between the hemistichs, given the 3rd sg.

jagh─Б╠Бna in 8d, but this is hardly unprecedented – and note that it returns abruptly to 2nd ps. in vs. 9. I therefore prefer to interpret 8ab as couched in the 2nd sg., as in the published translation But if a 3rd sg. reading of ├бp─Бс╕е is really desirable, I would prefer to consider the -s ending a local analogy to the precative pey─Бс╕е at the end of 3b, reinforced by the ambig. parallel ├бghaс╕е, rather than setting up an s-aorist stem to account for a single form.

I follow Geldner in taking both k─Бr├бm and bh├бram as the direct speech expression of a victory cry. The former is appropriate to gaming contexts, while the latter is at home in battles. Our ahvanta тАж bh├бram has a compositional equivalent bh├бra-h┼лti-, for which see comm. ad I.129.2; for k─Бr├бm тИЪkс╣Ы, see I.131.5. It may be convenient to assemble here some passages containing both bh├бra- and k─Бr├б- (or derivatives): I.l12.1 y─Б╠Бbhir [┼лt├нbhiс╕е] bh├бre k─Бr├бm ├бс╣Г┼Ы─Бya j├нnvathaс╕е; VIII.66.1 (likewise an Indra hymn): (├нndram … ┼лt├бye/ ……/) huv├й bh├бram n├б k─Бr├нс╣Зam; IX.16.5 mah├й bh├бr─Бya k─Бr├нс╣Зaс╕е; IX.14.1 k─Бr├бс╣Г b├нbhrat puruspс╣Ы╠Бham. See also Wackernagel KlSch. 340ff.

Griffith

When thou three hundred buffaloes’ flesh hadst eaten, and drunk, as Maghavan, three lakes of Soma,
All the Gods raised as ’twere a shout of triumph to Indra praise because he slew the Dragon.

Geldner

Als er das Fleisch von dreihundert B├╝ffeln gegessen, als der Gabenreiche drei Seen voll Soma getrunken hatte, da riefen die G├╢tter dem Indra “Sieg” zu, wie man “Gewinn” zuruft, als er den Drachen erschlagen hatte.

Grassmann

Als der dreihundert B├╝ffel Fleisch du assest, drei Seen Soma’s, m├дchtiger, du austrankst, Da riefen Heil dem Indra alle G├╢tter, wie Siegsgesang, da er erschlug die Schlange.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬWhen, Indra, you and U┼Ыanas, with vigorous and rapid courses went to the dwelling of Kutsa, then destroying his foes, you went in one chariot with Kutsa and the gods, and verily you have slain ┼Ъuс╣гс╣ЗaтАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When, Indra, (you and Kutsa) drove to the home of U┼Ыan─Б with the mighty, speeding horses,
as combatant you drove there on the same chariot with Kutsa, with the gods. You combated ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On u┼Ы├бn─Б as an indeclinable, see my 2007 тАЬVedic U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya and Avestan Kauui Usan: On the Morphology of the NamesтАЭ (Fs. Jasanoff).

On the basis of other mentions of this myth, 2nd du. ├бy─Бtam must conceal a V─Бyav Indra┼Ы ca type construction, with the other subject, beside voc. indra, being Kutsa. Cf. nearby dual dvandva indr─Б-kuts─Б (V.31.9). The gapping of Kutsa in the first half of the verse is repaired by cd sar├бthaс╣Г yay─Бtha, k├║tsena, with the same root тИЪy─Б as in ├бy─Бtam. I do not understand the change in tense stem.

Griffith

What time ye came with strong steeds swiftly speeding, O Usana and Indra, to the dwelling,
Thou camest thither -conquering together with Kutsa and the Gods: thou slewest Susna.

Als U├зana und Indra mit den starken, den raschgetriebnen Rossen ihr ins Haus kamt, Fuhrst siegreich du mit Kutsa und den G├╢ttern in gleichem Wagen, schlugst in Flucht den ├Зuschna.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou have formerly detached one wheel (of the car) of S┼лrya; another you have given to Kutsa wherewith to acquire wealth; with the thunderbolt you have confounded the voiceless Dasyus, you have destroyed in battle the speech-bereft (foes).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Confounded with voiceless dasyus: an─Бso dasy┼лn amс╣Ыс╣Зaс╕е: an─Бsa = asyarahit─Бn, devoid or deprived of words, asya, face or mouth, being put by metonymy for ┼Ыabda, the sound that comes from the mouth, articulate speech; Dasyus are also called amс╣Ыdhrav─Бcas = hiс╣Гsita v─Бgindriyan = having defective organs of speech

Jamison Brereton

You tore off the one wheel of the Sun for Kutsa; the other you made into wide space for driving.
You crushed the Dasyus mouthless with your murderous weapon; you wrenched those of slighting speech down into a woeful womb.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In the published translation I take k├║ts─Бya primarily with p─Бda a, though syntactically and metrically it should go with b. I would now emend the tr. to тАЬthe other you made into wide space for Kutsa to driveтАЭ or тАЬтАж for Kutsa for driving.тАЭ IтАЩm not sure how a wheel can become a wide space – what sounds like a kind of highway – but the addition of Kutsa doesnтАЩt make it any less comprehensible.

I take an─Б╠Бsaс╕е тАШmouthlessтАЩ as proleptic, describing the state of the Dasyus after Indra has finished crushing them (sim. to I.32.6 *an─Б╠Бс╕е pipiс╣гe), while Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н] take it as a standing characteristic of the Dasyus (тАЬmouthless DasyusтАЭ). There is no way to tell.

Griffith

One car-wheel of the Sun thou rolledst forward, and one thou settest free to move for Kutsa.
Thou slewest noseless Dasyus with thy weapon, and in their home o’erthrewest hostile speakers.

Geldner

Das eine Rad der Sonne rissest du ab, f├╝r Kutsa lie├Яest du das andere heil davonkommen. Du zerschmettertest die mundlosen Dasyu┬┤s mit der Waffe, du warfst die Mi├Яredenden ins Grab.

Grassmann

Du rolltest vor das eine Rad der Sonne, und triebst das andre an zum Heil des Kutsa, Erschlugst mit Blitz die h├дsslichen D├дmonen, und strecktest hin in ihrem Haus die Schm├дher.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the praises of Gauriv─лti exalt you; you have humbled Pipru for the son of Vidathin; с╣Ъji┼Ыvan preparing dressed viands, has, through your friendship brought you (to his presence), and you have drunk of his libation.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The praises of Gauriv─лti strengthened you. You made Pipru subject to Vaidathina.
R╠еji┼Ыvan brought you here for companionship, cooking cooked foods (for you). You drank his soma.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The etym. fig. p├бcan pakt─л╠Бс╕е is also a proleptic expression of sorts, тАЬcooking (food, so that it is) cooked,тАЭ though since pakt├н- is not an adj./participle, but a noun identifying a type of food, the parallel isnтАЩt exact. For other exx. of pakt├н- тИЪpac, see IV.24.7, VII.32.8.

Griffith

The lauds of Gauriviti made thee mighty to Vidathin’s son, as prey, thou gavest Pipru.
Rjisivan drew thee into friendship dressing the sacred food, and thou hast drunk his Soma.

Geldner

Die Loblieder des Gauriviti erbauten dich; du unterwarfst den Pipru dem Vaidathina. Rijisvan hatte dich zur Freundschaft gewonnen, indem er Kochspeise kochte. Du trankst seinen Soma.

Grassmann

Dich kr├дftigten des Gauriviti Lieder, Vidathin’s Sohne gabst du hin dem Pipru; Dich schafft’ herbei Ridschi├зvan sich zum Beistand, dir Br├╝hen kochend, seinen Soma trankst du.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThe observers of the nine month’s celebration, those of the ten months, pouring out libations, worship Indra with hymns; the leaders (of rites), glorifying him, have set open the cave (concealing the cattle).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The Navagvas, the Da┼Ыagvas [=Aс╣Еgirases], having pressed soma, chant to Indra with chants.
Just that cowpen with its covering [=Vala cave]тАФjust that have the men, having ritually labored, opened up.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. brings the third repetition of arcanti (1c, 6c [or ├бrcan(t); see above]; cf. ─Б╠Бrcan 2b).

I donтАЩt quite understand the double cid construction in cd, where even one cid seems somewhat superfluous. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take it as concessive and logically to be construed with apidh─Б╠Бnavantam (тАЬthe cowpen, although it had a coverтАЭ [Geldner: тАЬobwohl verschlossen,тАЭ sim. Witzel Got┼Н]). This is possible, though I donтАЩt like the position of cid, and I would also note that #g├бvyaс╣Г cid ┼лrv├бm is also found in VII.90.4, where a concessive value is harder to wring out.

Griffith

Navagvas and Dasgvas with libations of Soma juice sing hymns of praise to Indra.
Labouring at their task the men laid open the stall of Kine though firmly closed and fastened.

Die Navagva┬┤s, die Dasagva┬┤s haben Soma gepre├Яt und besingen den Indra mit Ges├дngen. Den Rinderpferch, obwohl verschlossen, brachen trotzdem die M├дnner auf, nachdem sie den Opferdienst versehen hatten.

Grassmann

Die Neuner und die Zehner, Soma kelternd, besingen ihn, den Indra, mit Ges├дngen; Den Stall der K├╝he auch, den festverschlossnen, erbrachen sie, die M├дnner, eifrig wirkend.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAlthough, knowing the heroic acts which, Maghavan, you have performed, how may I adequately offer you adoration; most mighty Indra, we ever celebrate sacred rites the recent exploits which you have achieved.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

How shall I, (though) knowing them, now encompass your heroic deeds that you have done, o bounteous one,
and the new ones that you will do, strongest one? We will proclaim
these (deeds) of yours at the ceremonies.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Grassmann, Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н), and Klein (DGRV I.219) interp. p├бri тИЪcar as тАШserveтАЩ.

Although this sense is found in later Vedic, the RVic instances of this lexeme only have the literal meaning тАШgo aroundтАЩ (e.g., III.7.2) with the developed sense тАШencompassтАЩ. (I.127.9 comes closest to тАШserveтАЩ, but the тАШsurroundтАЩ sense is dominant.) Interpreting p├бri car─Бс╣Зi here as тАШserveтАЩ requires the part. vidv─Б╠Бn to take an obj.

(тАЬknowing your heroic deeds тАжтАЭ), but p─Бda-final vidv─Б╠Бn is almost always used absolutely. Moreover ├бpar─лtaс╕е (p├бri тИЪi) in the next vs. continues the thought of conceptual circumscription. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) and Klein divide the vs. syntactically into ab / cd, with the rel. cl. of c expressing the obj. of d. By contrast I think the lexical parallelism and the conjunction co [=ca u] of тАж y─Б╠Бcak├бrtha / y─Б╠Бco тАж kс╣Ыс╣З├бvaс╕е of bc mark those relative clauses as tightly conjoined, and I take them as subordinate to p─Бda a. Further, the last p─Бda pr├йd u t─Б╠Бte vid├бtheс╣гu brav─Бma strikes me as a self-contained (pseudo- )refrain, reminiscent of the Gс╣Ыtsam─Бda refrain in II: bс╣Ыh├бd vadema vid├бthe suv─л╠Бr─Бс╕е (II.1.16d etc.).

Griffith

How shall I serve thee, Maghavan, though knowing full well what hero deeds thou hast accomplished?
And the fresh deeds which thou wilt do, Most Mighty! these, too, will we tell forth in sacred synods.

Geldner

Wie kann ich dir jetzt dienen, der ich die Heldentaten kenne, die du, Gabenreicher, getan hast? Auch die neuen, die du noch tun wirst, du Gewaltigster, die wollen wir von dir in weiser Rede verk├╝nden.

Grassmann

Wie muss ich jetzt im Geiste dich umwandern, die Thaten kennend, die du, M├дcht’ger, wirktest? Und was du neues thun noch wirst, o st├дrkster, das wollen auch wir preisen bei den Festen.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗрдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдЕрдкрд░реАрддрдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрднрд┐рд░рдкрд░рд┐рдЧрддрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдЬрдиреБрд╖рд╛ рдЬрдирдирд╕рд┐рджреНрдзреЗрдирд╛рддреНрдореАрдпреЗрдирд╡реАрд░реНрдпреЗрдгрдмрд▓реЗрдирднреВрд░рд┐ рднреВрд░реАрдгрд┐ рдмрд╣реВрдирд┐рдПрддрд╛ рдПрддрд╛рдирд┐ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖реЗрдгреЛрдкрд▓рднреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдирд┐ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд┐ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрддрд╛рдирд┐ рднреБрд╡рдирдЬрд╛рддрд╛рдирд┐ рдЪрдХреГрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдХреГрддрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╣реЗрд╡рдЬреНрд░рд┐рдиреН рд╡рдЬреНрд░рд╡рдиреНрдирд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░ рджрдзреБрд╖реНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╕рдкрддреНрдирд╛рдиреН рдзрд░реНрд╖рдпрдВрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдиреБрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдВ рдпрд╛рдЪрд┐рддреН рдпрд╛рдирд┐рдЪ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд┐ рдХреГрдгрд╡рдГ рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рдГ рддреЗрддреНрд╡рджреАрдпрд╕реНрдпрддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрддрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ рддрд╕реНрдпрдмрд▓рд╕реНрдпрд╡рд░реНрддрд╛ рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд░рдпрд┐рддрд╛ рдирдХреЛрдкреНрдпрд╕реНрддрд┐ рее резрек рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬUnmatched (by any), you have done, Indra, all these many (deeds) by your innate energy; wielder of the thunderbolt, whatever you, the humbler of (foes), have undertaken, there is no one the arrester of this your prowess.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Having done all these many (deeds), Indra, by your nature you cannot be circumscribed in heroism.
As for those (deeds) you will do even now in your daring, possessor of the maceтАФthere exists no one to obstruct this power of yours.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is structured somewhat like vs. 13, with (a) et─Б╠Бv├н┼Ыv─Б cakс╣Ыv─Б╠Бn corresponding to (13b) (v─лry─Б╠А) тАж y─Б╠Бcak├бrtha, though with pf. participle not rel. cl., and (c) y─Б╠Бcid n├║ тАж kс╣Ыс╣З├бvaс╕е corresponding even more closely to (13c) y─Б╠Бco n├║ тАж kс╣Ыс╣З├бvaс╕е. I would therefore now slightly emend the published translation to reflect this parallelism more closely: тАЬBy your nature you cannot be circumscribed in heroism – you, Indra, (as one) having done all these many (deeds) (as well as) those (deeds) that you will do even now in your daring. There exists no one to obstruct this power of yours.тАЭ In other words I take p─Бdas a and c as parallel adjunct expressions, with b as their joint main clause, and d (like 13d) independent. Note that d has no overt referent for y─Б╠Бin c. The English is awkward, but this structure corresponds better to the Skt.

Griffith

Resistless from of old through hero courage, thou hast done all these many acts, O Indra.
What thou wilt do in bravery, Thunder-wielder! none is there who may hinder this thy prowess.

Geldner

Nachdem du, Indra, diese vielen Taten getan hast, schon bei der Geburt an Heldenkraft unerreicht, gibt es keinen, der deiner Kraft wehren wird, was du auch wagemutig noch tun wirst, du Keulentr├дger.

Grassmann

Der, Indra, du dies alles reichlich thatest, mit Heldenkraft von Haus aus unbezwinglich; Was k├╝hn, o Blitzer, noch du wirst vollbringen, darin kann niemand deine Kraftthat hemmen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMost mighty Indra, be plural ased to accept the prayers which we are about to offer, and the present praises which we repeat; firm, doing pious acts, and desirous of wealth; I have fabricated acceptable and pious works like (rich) garments, and like a chariot.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Like garments and like a chariot: praises and hymns, are compared to gaments, as being fit to be received as a respectful present, upasaс╣Гh─Бravad gr─Бhy─Бni; the same are compared to a chariot, as the means of conveying Indra and the gods to sacrifices

Jamison Brereton

O Indra, enjoy the sacred formulations being made, the new ones we have made for you, strongest one.
Like garments, lovely and well made, like a chariot have I fashioned themтАФI the clever artisan, seeking goods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the sandhi in n├бvy─Б ├бkarma see Oldenberg

Griffith

Indra, accept the prayers which now are offered, accept the new prayers, Mightiest! which we utter.
Like fair and well-made robes, I, seeking riches, as a deft craftsman makes a car, have wrought them.

Indra, erfreue dich an den bereiteten Erbauungen, die wir dir aufs neue bereitet haben, du Gewaltigster! Wie sch├╢ne Kleider wohlgearbeitet habe ich sie, Gut w├╝nschend, wie ein kunstfertiger Meister einen Wagen gezimmert.

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ ! рд╡рдВрд╢ рдФрд░ рдзрди рдХреА рдЖрд╢рд╛ рд╕реЗ рдЖрдк рд▓реЛрдЧ рдЖрд▓рд╕реНрдп рд╕реЗ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрде рдХрд╛ рди рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧ рдХрд░реЛ, рдХрд┐рдиреНрддреБ рдирд┐рддреНрдп рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрде рдХреА рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐ рд╕реЗ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдп рдХреА рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐ рдХрд░рдХреЗ рд╡рд╕реНрддреНрд░ рдФрд░ рд░рде рд╕реЗ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╕реБрдЦ рдХрд╛ рднреЛрдЧ рдХрд░рдХреЗ рдирд╡реАрди рдпрд╢ рдкреНрд░рдХрдЯ рдХрд░реЛ реерезрелрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕ рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рдЙрдирддреАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдкрдЪреНрдЪреАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╢рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдареЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ ! рдпрд╕реНрдп рддреЗ рдирд╡реНрдпрд╛рдГ рд╢реНрд░рд┐рдпреЛ рд╡рдпрдордХрд░реНрдо рдпрд╛ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрдорд╛рдгрд╛ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо рддреНрд╡рдВ рдЬреБрд╖рд╕реНрд╡ рддрд╛ рднрджреНрд░рд╛ рд╕реБрдХреГрддрд╛ рд╡рд╕реНрддреНрд░реЗрд╡ рд╕реНрд╡рдкрд╛ рдзреАрд░реЛ рд╡рд╕реВрдпреВ рд░рдердВ рди рднрджреНрд░рд╛ рд╕реБрдХреГрддрд╛ рдЕрд╣рдорддрдХреНрд╖рдореН реерезрелрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрде рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╖рдпреЗ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдерд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдпреБрдХреНрдд (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо) рдЕрдиреНрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ рд╡рд╛ред рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдореЗрддреНрдпрдиреНрдирдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрдард┐рддрдореНред (рдирд┐рдШрдВрежреи.рен) (рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрдорд╛рдгрд╛) рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреЗрди рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛рдирд┐ (рдЬреБрд╖рд╕реНрд╡) рд╕реЗрд╡рд╕реНрд╡ (рдпрд╛) рдпрд╛рдирд┐ (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рд╢рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрда) рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рдмрд▓рдпреБрдХреНрдд (рдирд╡реНрдпрд╛рдГ) рдирд╡реАрдирд╛рдГ рд╢реНрд░рд┐рдпрдГ (рдЕрдХрд░реНрдо) рдХреБрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рдо (рд╡рд╕реНрддреНрд░реЗрд╡) рдпрдерд╛ рд╡рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рддрдерд╛ (рднрджреНрд░рд╛) рдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдгрдХрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ (рд╕реБрдХреГрддрд╛) рдзрд░реНрдореНрдпреЗрдг рдирд┐рд╖реНрдкрд╛рджрд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐ (рд╡рд╕реВрдпреБрдГ) рдЖрддреНрдордиреЛ рдзрдирдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫреБрдГ (рд░рдердореН) рд░рдордгреАрдпрдореН (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рдзреАрд░рдГ) рдзреНрдпрд╛рдирд╡рд╛рдиреН рдпреЛрдЧреА (рд╕реНрд╡рдкрд╛рдГ) рд╕рддреНрдпрднрд╛рд╖рдгрд╛рджрд┐рдХрд░реНрдорд╛ (рдЕрддрдХреНрд╖рдореН) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рдореН реерезрелрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ ! рдЧреЛрддреНрд░рдзрдирд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╢рдпрд╛ рдпреВрдпрдорд╛рд▓рд╕реНрдпреЗрди рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдердВ рдорд╛ рддреНрдпрдЬрдд, рдХрд┐рдиреНрддреБ рдирд┐рддреНрдпрдВ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдерд╡рд░реНрдзрдиреЗрдиреИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдВ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдпрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╡рджреНрд░рдерд╡рддреНрд╕реБрдЦрдВ рднреБрдХреНрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдиреВрддрдирдВ рдпрд╢рдГ рдкреНрд░рдердпрддреЗрддрд┐ реерезрелрее рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХреЛрдирд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддрд┐рддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рд╣реЗ рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреЛ ! рдореЛрд╣ рд╡ рдзрди рдпрд╛рдВрдЪреНрдпрд╛ рдЖрд╢реЗрдиреЗ рддреБрдореНрд╣реА рдЖрд│рд╢реА рдмрдиреВрди рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдЪрд╛ рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧ рдХрд░реВ рдирдХрд╛, рддрд░ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдЪреА рд╡реГрджреНрдзреА рдХрд░реВрди рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рд╡рд╛рдврд╡рд╛. рд╡рд╕реНрддреНрд░ рд╡ рд░рде рдпрд╛рдВрдЪреНрдпрд╛рдореБрд│реЗ рд╕реБрдЦ рднреЛрдЧрддрд╛ рдпреЗрддреЗ рддрд╕реЗ рд╕реБрдЦ рднреЛрдЧреВрди рдирд╡реАрди рдпрд╢ рдорд┐рд│рд╡рд╛. рее резрел рее
